## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models relate growth rate to current population through density-dependent feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/microbial populations)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak/multiplicative): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (cooperative growth at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy growth-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (1 + c3) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional/anomalous growth kinetics)
- Beverton-Holt continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with contest competition minus mortality)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (resource depletion over time)
- Linear density dependence with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (logistic growth plus constant immigration)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density feedback)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Growth rate proportional to population (dP_dt ~ P) indicates density-independent exponential regime
- Growth rate with P*(1-P/K) structure indicates negative density-dependent feedback and carrying capacity
- Cubic terms in P (Pآ³ or Pآ²*(1-P/K)) suggest Allee effects or cooperative/competitive interactions
- Logarithmic dependence on P (P*log(K/P)) indicates Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where decline is slower than rise
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+P)) suggests contest competition or resource saturation at individual level
- Time-dependent coefficients (e.g., exp(-c*t) multipliers) indicate changing environmental conditions or resource depletion
- Sign change in dP_dt at intermediate P values indicates bistability or Allee threshold dynamics
- Fractional powers of P (P^c with 0<c<1) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling or diffusion-limited growth
- Product of multiple (P - threshold) factors indicates multiple equilibria in population dynamics
- Periodic functions of time multiplying growth terms indicate seasonal or circadian environmental forcing
